<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">2006 Pacific hurricane season</h1>
<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
<div class="noprint" id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"></div>
<div class="mw-jump" id="jump-to-nav">

<td class="hlist noprint nowrap" colspan="2" style="text-align:center;border-top: 1px solid #aaa; padding-top: 3px;"><a href="/wiki/Pacific_hurricane" title="Pacific hurricane">Pacific hurricane seasons</a><br/>
<a href="/wiki/2004_Pacific_hurricane_season" title="2004 Pacific hurricane season">2004</a>, <a href="/wiki/2005_Pacific_hurricane_season" title="2005 Pacific hurricane season">2005</a>, <b>2006</b>, <a href="/wiki/2007_Pacific_hurricane_season" title="2007 Pacific hurricane season">2007</a>, <a href="/wiki/2008_Pacific_hurricane_season" title="2008 Pacific hurricane season">2008</a></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>The <b>2006 Pacific hurricane season</b> was the most active since <a href="/wiki/2000_Pacific_hurricane_season" title="2000 Pacific hurricane season">2000</a>, producing 19 <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone" title="Tropical cyclone">tropical storms</a> or hurricanes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-epachurdat_1-0"><a href="#cite_note-epachurdat-1">[1]</a></sup> Eighteen developed within the <a href="/wiki/National_Hurricane_Center" title="National Hurricane Center">National Hurricane Center</a> (NHC) area of warning responsibility, which is east of <a href="/wiki/140th_meridian_west" title="140th meridian west">140°W</a>, and one storm formed between <a href="/wiki/140th_meridian_west" title="140th meridian west">140°W</a> and the <a href="/wiki/International_Date_Line" title="International Date Line">International Date Line</a>, which is under the jurisdiction of the <a href="/wiki/Central_Pacific_Hurricane_Center" title="Central Pacific Hurricane Center">Central Pacific Hurricane Center</a> (CPHC). Of the 19 total storms, eleven became hurricanes, of which six attained <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone_scales" title="Tropical cyclone scales">major hurricane status</a>. Within the NHC portion of the basin, the season officially began on May 15, and in the CPHC portion, it started on June 1; the season officially ended on November 30. These dates conventionally delimit the period of each year when most tropical cyclones form in the eastern <a href="/wiki/Pacific_hurricane" title="Pacific hurricane">Pacific basin</a>.</p>
<p>The strongest storm of the season was <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Ioke" title="Hurricane Ioke">Hurricane Ioke</a>, which reached <a href="/wiki/List_of_Category_5_Pacific_hurricanes" title="List of Category 5 Pacific hurricanes">Category 5</a> status on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saffir-Simpson_Hurricane_Scale" title="Saffir-Simpson Hurricane Scale">Saffir-Simpson scale</a> in the central Pacific Ocean; Ioke passed near <a href="/wiki/Johnston_Atoll" title="Johnston Atoll">Johnston Atoll</a> and later <a href="/wiki/Wake_Island" title="Wake Island">Wake Island</a>, where it caused heavy damage but no deaths. The deadliest storm of the season was <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_John_(2006)" title="Hurricane John (2006)">Hurricane John</a>, which killed six people after striking the <a href="/wiki/Baja_California_Peninsula" title="Baja California Peninsula">Baja California Peninsula</a>, and the costliest storm was <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Lane_(2006)" title="Hurricane Lane (2006)">Hurricane Lane</a>, which caused $203 million in damage in southwestern Mexico (2006 <a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">USD</a>, $241 million 2017 USD).</p>
<p>Seasonal activity began on May 27, when <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Aletta_(2006)" title="Tropical Storm Aletta (2006)">Tropical Storm Aletta</a> formed off the southwest coast of Mexico. No storms formed in June, though the season became active in July when five named storms developed, including <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Daniel_(2006)" title="Hurricane Daniel (2006)">Hurricane Daniel</a> which was the second strongest storm of the season, as well as <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Emilia_(2006)" title="Tropical Storm Emilia (2006)">Tropical Storm Emilia</a>. During August, Hurricanes Ioke and John formed, as well as four other storms. September was a relatively quiet month with two storms, of which one was Hurricane Lane. Three storms developed in October including <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Paul_(2006)" title="Hurricane Paul (2006)">Hurricane Paul</a> and two formed in November; this marked the second time on record, after <a href="/wiki/1961_Pacific_hurricane_season" title="1961 Pacific hurricane season">1961</a>, when more than one tropical storm developed in the basin during the month of November.</p>
<p></p>

<td align="left"><b>Actual activity</b></td>
<td>18</td>
<td>10</td>
<td>5</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>On May 22, 2006, the <a href="/wiki/National_Oceanic_and_Atmospheric_Administration" title="National Oceanic and Atmospheric Administration">National Oceanic and Atmospheric Administration</a>'s (NOAA) <a href="/wiki/Climate_Prediction_Center" title="Climate Prediction Center">CPC</a> (CPC) released their forecasts for the 2006 <a href="/wiki/2006_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="2006 Atlantic hurricane season">Atlantic</a> and Pacific hurricane seasons. The Pacific season was expected to be hindered by the decades-long cycle that began in <a href="/wiki/1995_Pacific_hurricane_season" title="1995 Pacific hurricane season">1995</a>, which generally increased <a href="/wiki/Wind_shear" title="Wind shear">wind shear</a> across the basin. NOAA predicted a below-normal level of activity in the Eastern Pacific, with 12–16 named storms, of which 6–8 were expected to become hurricanes, and 1–3 expected to become major hurricanes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NOAA_May_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-NOAA_May-3">[3]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Central_Pacific_Hurricane_Center" title="Central Pacific Hurricane Center">Central Pacific Hurricane Center</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Area_of_responsibility" title="Area of responsibility">area of responsibility</a> was also expected to be below average, with only two to three tropical cyclones expected to form or cross into the area.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NOAA_May_CP_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-NOAA_May_CP-4">[4]</a></sup> They expected that neither <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/El_Ni%C3%B1o_Southern_Oscillation" title="El Niño Southern Oscillation">El Niño</a> nor La Niña would affect conditions significantly.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NOAA_May_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-NOAA_May-3">[3]</a></sup></p>
<p>On May 15, the hurricane season began in the Eastern Pacific basin, which is the area of the northern <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean" title="Pacific Ocean">Pacific Ocean</a> east of 140°<a href="/wiki/Longitude" title="Longitude">W</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> On June 1, the season began in the Central Pacific warning zone (between 140°<a href="/wiki/Longitude" title="Longitude">W</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/International_Dateline" title="International Dateline">International Dateline</a>); however, no storms occurred in the region until July.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Seasonal_summary">Seasonal summary</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Seasonal summary">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_the_2006_Pacific_hurricane_season" title="Timeline of the 2006 Pacific hurricane season">Timeline of the 2006 Pacific hurricane season</a></div>
<center>
<div class="timeline-wrapper"><map id="timeline_a8c4a7ec999ba84e900d57a2c6c05ce5" name="timeline_a8c4a7ec999ba84e900d57a2c6c05ce5">
<area alt="Hurricane Paul (2006)" coords="641,57,727,77" href="/wiki/Hurricane_Paul_(2006)" shape="rect" title="Hurricane Paul (2006)"/>
<area alt="Hurricane Lane (2006)" coords="502,69,588,90" href="/wiki/Hurricane_Lane_(2006)" shape="rect" title="Hurricane Lane (2006)"/>
<area alt="Hurricane John (2006)" coords="452,44,539,65" href="/wiki/Hurricane_John_(2006)" shape="rect" title="Hurricane John (2006)"/>
<area alt="Hurricane Ioke" coords="424,20,510,41" href="/wiki/Hurricane_Ioke" shape="rect" title="Hurricane Ioke"/>
<area alt="Saffir-Simpson Hurricane Scale" coords="602,170,804,190" href="/wiki/Saffir%2DSimpson_Hurricane_Scale" shape="rect" title="Saffir-Simpson Hurricane Scale"/></map><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/timeline/a8c4a7ec999ba84e900d57a2c6c05ce5.png" usemap="#timeline_a8c4a7ec999ba84e900d57a2c6c05ce5"/></div>
</center>
<p>No tropical storms developed in June in the basin, which was unusual compared to the average of two storms forming during the month. Since 1966, there have been only three other seasons in which a tropical storm did not form in June, these being <a href="/wiki/1969_Pacific_hurricane_season" title="1969 Pacific hurricane season">1969</a>, <a href="/wiki/2004_Pacific_hurricane_season" title="2004 Pacific hurricane season">2004</a>, and <a href="/wiki/2007_Pacific_hurricane_season" title="2007 Pacific hurricane season">2007</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> After such an inactive month, the tropics became active in July when five named storms developed, including <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Daniel_(2006)" title="Hurricane Daniel (2006)">Hurricane Daniel</a> which was the second strongest storm of the season. During August, Hurricanes Ioke and John formed, as well as four other storms. September was a relatively quiet month with two storms, of which one was Hurricane Lane.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EPAC_HURDAT_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-EPAC_HURDAT-8">[8]</a></sup> By that time, however, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/El_Ni%C3%B1o-Southern_Oscillation" title="El Niño-Southern Oscillation">El Niño</a> conditions became established across the Pacific,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cphc_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-cphc-9">[9]</a></sup> which is known to enhance <a href="/wiki/Pacific_hurricane" title="Pacific hurricane">Pacific hurricane</a> activity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NOAA_May_3-2"><a href="#cite_note-NOAA_May-3">[3]</a></sup></p>
<p>Three storms developed in October, including Hurricane Paul. <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EPAC_HURDAT_8-1"><a href="#cite_note-EPAC_HURDAT-8">[8]</a></sup> Tropical activity within the basin in November 2006 was the most active on record, based on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Accumulated_Cyclone_Energy" title="Accumulated Cyclone Energy">Accumulated Cyclone Energy</a> (ACE) Index. Three tropical cyclones formed, of which two became tropical storms; only two other seasons on record, <a href="/wiki/1961_Pacific_hurricane_season" title="1961 Pacific hurricane season">1961</a> and <a href="/wiki/2015_Pacific_hurricane_season" title="2015 Pacific hurricane season">2015</a>, produced two tropical storms in the month of November.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nov06_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-nov06-10">[10]</a></sup> In addition, Mexico was struck by four tropical cyclones in 2006, none on the Atlantic coast and all along the Pacific coast.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wmo_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-wmo-11">[11]</a></sup> One hit <a href="/wiki/Baja_California_Peninsula" title="Baja California Peninsula">Baja California Peninsula</a> while the others made landfall on the mainland.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EPAC_Book_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-EPAC_Book-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<p>An <a href="/wiki/Extratropical_cyclone" title="Extratropical cyclone">extratropical</a> storm persisted in the extreme northern central Pacific Ocean in late October. It drifted over unusually <a href="/wiki/Sea_surface_temperature" title="Sea surface temperature">warm waters</a> up to 3.6 °F (2 °C) above normal, and gradually developed convection near the center. By November 2, <a href="/wiki/QuikSCAT" title="QuikSCAT">QuikSCAT</a> satellite suggested the system attained winds of up to 60 mph (95 km/h) about 900 mi (1450 km) west of <a href="/wiki/Oregon" title="Oregon">Oregon</a>. The system also developed an <a href="/wiki/Eye_(cyclone)" title="Eye (cyclone)">eye</a> and an eyewall. The cyclone tracked northeastward as it gradually weakened, and dissipated on November 4. <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">NASA</a> considered the cyclone to be a <a href="/wiki/Subtropical_cyclone" title="Subtropical cyclone">subtropical storm</a>. However, as it formed outside of the territory of any monitoring organization, it was not named. Operationally, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Navy" title="United States Navy">United States Navy</a> treated the system as a tropical disturbance, numbered 91C.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NASA-91C_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-NASA-91C-13">[13]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Systems">Systems</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Systems">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Storm_Aletta">Tropical Storm Aletta</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Tropical Storm Aletta">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #00faf4">Tropical storm (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tropical_Storm_Aletta_(2006).jpg"><img alt="Tropical Storm Aletta (2006).jpg" data-file-height="4000" data-file-width="4000" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Tropical_Storm_Aletta_%282006%29.jpg/150px-Tropical_Storm_Aletta_%282006%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Tropical_Storm_Aletta_%282006%29.jpg/225px-Tropical_Storm_Aletta_%282006%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Tropical_Storm_Aletta_%282006%29.jpg/300px-Tropical_Storm_Aletta_%282006%29.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Aletta_2006_track.png"><img alt="Aletta 2006 track.png" data-file-height="633" data-file-width="1024" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Aletta_2006_track.png/150px-Aletta_2006_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Aletta_2006_track.png/225px-Aletta_2006_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Aletta_2006_track.png/300px-Aletta_2006_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>May 27 – May 30</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>45 mph (75 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  1002 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Aletta_(2006)" title="Tropical Storm Aletta (2006)">Tropical Storm Aletta (2006)</a></div>
<p>On May 27, 12 days into the season, Tropical Depression One formed about 190 miles (305 km) south of Acapulco.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-atcr_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-atcr-14">[14]</a></sup> It slowly organized and became a tropical storm with 45 mph (75 km/h) sustained winds.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-atcr_14-1"><a href="#cite_note-atcr-14">[14]</a></sup> While named tropical cyclones in May are infrequent events, Aletta marked the seventh consecutive year to have a named cyclone form in May.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NHC_May_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-NHC_May-15">[15]</a></sup> The storm moved toward the <a href="/wiki/Guerrero" title="Guerrero">Guerrero</a> coast in southwestern Mexico, prompting the Mexican government to issue <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tropical_storm_watch" title="Tropical storm watch">tropical storm watches</a> between <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Punta_Maldonado&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Punta Maldonado (page does not exist)">Punta Maldonado</a> and <a href="/wiki/Zihuatanejo" title="Zihuatanejo">Zihuatanejo</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SMN_Aletta_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-SMN_Aletta-16">[16]</a></sup> Aletta then became stationary over the <a href="/wiki/Guerrero" title="Guerrero">Guerrero</a> and <a href="/wiki/Oaxaca" title="Oaxaca">Oaxaca</a> coastlines, but it later turned to the west and dissipated on May 30.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-atcr_14-2"><a href="#cite_note-atcr-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<p>Aletta produced moderate rainfall across Mexico, including a 24-hour rainfall total of 3.94 inches (100 mm)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[nb 1]</a></sup> in Jacatepec, Oaxaca on May 30, and 3.78 inches (96 mm) in La Calera, Guerrero, the next day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SMN_Aletta_16-1"><a href="#cite_note-SMN_Aletta-16">[16]</a></sup> There were no reports of damage, flooding, or casualties.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-atcr_14-3"><a href="#cite_note-atcr-14">[14]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NHC_May_15-1"><a href="#cite_note-NHC_May-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Depression_Two-E">Tropical Depression Two-E</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Tropical Depression Two-E">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #5ebaff">Tropical depression (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tropical_Depression_Two-E_(2006).PNG"><img alt="Tropical Depression Two-E (2006).PNG" data-file-height="652" data-file-width="730" height="134" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Tropical_Depression_Two-E_%282006%29.PNG/150px-Tropical_Depression_Two-E_%282006%29.PNG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Tropical_Depression_Two-E_%282006%29.PNG/225px-Tropical_Depression_Two-E_%282006%29.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Tropical_Depression_Two-E_%282006%29.PNG/300px-Tropical_Depression_Two-E_%282006%29.PNG 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Two-E_2006_track.png"><img alt="Two-E 2006 track.png" data-file-height="633" data-file-width="1024" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Two-E_2006_track.png/150px-Two-E_2006_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Two-E_2006_track.png/225px-Two-E_2006_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Two-E_2006_track.png/300px-Two-E_2006_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>June 3 – June 5</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>35 mph (55 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  1005 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Depression_Two-E_(2006)" title="Tropical Depression Two-E (2006)">Tropical Depression Two-E (2006)</a></div>
<p>On the day after Aletta dissipated, a new area of disturbed weather developed off the southwest Mexican coast. High shear slowed the development of the system, although it gained enough convection and organization to be classified as a tropical depression on June 3. The depression strengthened to near tropical storm status as it approached the coast of southwestern Mexico; however, shear persisted over the system and it weakened before dissipating on June 4.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2tcr_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-2tcr-18">[17]</a></sup></p>
<p>Despite never becoming a named storm, heavy rain occurred, including a total of 19.13 inches (486 mm) measured in a 48‑hour period in Acapulco.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[18]</a></sup> Mudslides and flash flooding were reported,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2tcr_18-1"><a href="#cite_note-2tcr-18">[17]</a></sup> forcing 72 people from their homes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[19]</a></sup> No deaths or serious damage was reported.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2tcr_18-2"><a href="#cite_note-2tcr-18">[17]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hurricane_Bud">Hurricane Bud</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Hurricane Bud">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Bud_(2006)" title="Hurricane Bud (2006)">Hurricane Bud (2006)</a></div>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ffc140">Category 3 hurricane (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_bud_2006.jpg"><img alt="Hurricane bud 2006.jpg" data-file-height="4000" data-file-width="4000" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Hurricane_bud_2006.jpg/150px-Hurricane_bud_2006.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Hurricane_bud_2006.jpg/225px-Hurricane_bud_2006.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Hurricane_bud_2006.jpg/300px-Hurricane_bud_2006.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bud_2006_track.png"><img alt="Bud 2006 track.png" data-file-height="633" data-file-width="1024" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Bud_2006_track.png/150px-Bud_2006_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Bud_2006_track.png/225px-Bud_2006_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Bud_2006_track.png/300px-Bud_2006_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>July 11 – July 16</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>125 mph (205 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  953 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>On July 11, after over a month of inactivity, a disturbance off the <a href="/wiki/Baja_California_Peninsula" title="Baja California Peninsula">Peninsula of Baja California</a> developed into a tropical depression. It moved west-northwestward for its entire duration, quickly intensifying into a tropical storm and hurricane. A clear, well-defined <a href="/wiki/Eye_(cyclone)" title="Eye (cyclone)">eye</a> developed, and Bud became the first <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone_scales" title="Tropical cyclone scales">major hurricane</a> of the season. On July 13, the hurricane attained peak winds of 125 mph (205 km/h), although cooler waters and stable air caused a marked weakening trend. By July 15, Bud weakened to tropical depression status, and the next day it degenerated into a remnant low pressure area.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[20]</a></sup> The remnants of Bud produced light rainfall across <a href="/wiki/Hawaii" title="Hawaii">Hawaii</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jul06_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-jul06-22">[21]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hurricane_Carlotta">Hurricane Carlotta</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Hurricane Carlotta">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ffffcc">Category 1 hurricane (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_carlotta_2006.jpg"><img alt="Hurricane carlotta 2006.jpg" data-file-height="5400" data-file-width="5400" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Hurricane_carlotta_2006.jpg/150px-Hurricane_carlotta_2006.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Hurricane_carlotta_2006.jpg/225px-Hurricane_carlotta_2006.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Hurricane_carlotta_2006.jpg/300px-Hurricane_carlotta_2006.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Carlotta_2006_track.png"><img alt="Carlotta 2006 track.png" data-file-height="633" data-file-width="1024" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Carlotta_2006_track.png/150px-Carlotta_2006_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Carlotta_2006_track.png/225px-Carlotta_2006_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Carlotta_2006_track.png/300px-Carlotta_2006_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>July 12 – July 16</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>85 mph (140 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  981 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>A tropical wave exited Africa on June 30 and moved across the Atlantic Ocean without development. On July 9, while crossing Central America into the eastern North Pacific Ocean, thunderstorm activity increased, and the system organized into Tropical Depression Four-E early on July 12 about 290 mi (465 km) south of <a href="/wiki/Zihuatanejo" title="Zihuatanejo">Zihuatanejo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guerrero" title="Guerrero">Guerrero</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tcr_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-tcr-23">[22]</a></sup> The large depression moved quickly to the west-northwest to the south of a <a href="/wiki/Ridge_(meteorology)" title="Ridge (meteorology)">ridge</a> over northwestern Mexico, and its outer rainbands moved across the coast. Rainfall totals were less than 1 inch (25 mm).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tcr_23-1"><a href="#cite_note-tcr-23">[22]</a></sup> The depression intensified into Tropical Storm Carlotta just six hours after forming.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tcr_23-2"><a href="#cite_note-tcr-23">[22]</a></sup> By late on July 12, the storm developed <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone#Physical_structure" title="Tropical cyclone">banding features</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[23]</a></sup> and early on July 13 Carlotta attained hurricane status about 430 mi (700 km) south of the southern tip of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baja_California_peninsula" title="Baja California peninsula">Baja California peninsula</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tcr_23-3"><a href="#cite_note-tcr-23">[22]</a></sup></p>
<p>As Carlotta intensified, the system became more compact, and it reached peak winds of 85 mph (140 km/h) on July 13.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tcr_23-4"><a href="#cite_note-tcr-23">[22]</a></sup> An <a href="/wiki/Eye_(cyclone)" title="Eye (cyclone)">eye</a> formed in the center, and the hurricane was briefly forecast to attain <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone_scales" title="Tropical cyclone scales">major hurricane</a> status, or a Category 3 on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saffir-Simpson_Hurricane_Scale" title="Saffir-Simpson Hurricane Scale">Saffir-Simpson scale</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[24]</a></sup> However, Carlotta weakened due to increased wind shear from <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Bud_(2006)" title="Hurricane Bud (2006)">Hurricane Bud</a> to its west,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tcr_23-5"><a href="#cite_note-tcr-23">[22]</a></sup> and the eye and convection deteriorated.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[25]</a></sup> Carlotta briefly weakened to tropical storm status late on July 14, although a decrease in shear allowed it to reintensify into a hurricane. This was short-lived as the center moved into the area of cooler waters, and Carlotta again weakened to tropical storm status.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tcr_23-6"><a href="#cite_note-tcr-23">[22]</a></sup> Late on July 15, the circulation became separated from the convection,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[26]</a></sup> and Carlotta weakened to tropical depression status on July 16, and the next day generated into a remnant low. The circulation continued generally westward, dissipating on July 20 about 1500 mi (2400 km) east of the Hawaiian islands.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tcr_23-7"><a href="#cite_note-tcr-23">[22]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hurricane_Daniel">Hurricane Daniel</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Hurricane Daniel">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ff8f20">Category 4 hurricane (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_daniel_2006.jpg"><img alt="Hurricane daniel 2006.jpg" data-file-height="4320" data-file-width="4320" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Hurricane_daniel_2006.jpg/150px-Hurricane_daniel_2006.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Hurricane_daniel_2006.jpg/225px-Hurricane_daniel_2006.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Hurricane_daniel_2006.jpg/300px-Hurricane_daniel_2006.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Daniel_2006_track.png"><img alt="Daniel 2006 track.png" data-file-height="633" data-file-width="1024" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Daniel_2006_track.png/150px-Daniel_2006_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Daniel_2006_track.png/225px-Daniel_2006_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Daniel_2006_track.png/300px-Daniel_2006_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>July 16 – July 26</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>150 mph (240 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  933 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Daniel_(2006)" title="Hurricane Daniel (2006)">Hurricane Daniel (2006)</a></div>
<p>On July 16, a tropical disturbance formed far to the south of the <a href="/wiki/Baja_California_Peninsula" title="Baja California Peninsula">Baja California Peninsula</a> and quickly increased in convective activity and organization, becoming a tropical depression. The system continued to organize and was designated as a tropical storm the next day. On July 18, Daniel attained hurricane status, and two days later underwent rapid intensification; it reached <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone_scales" title="Tropical cyclone scales">major hurricane status</a> and was later upgraded further to Category 4 status on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saffir-Simpson_Hurricane_Scale" title="Saffir-Simpson Hurricane Scale">Saffir-Simpson Hurricane Scale</a>. Its peak intensity was 150 mph (240 km/h).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-danieltcr_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-danieltcr-28">[27]</a></sup> The hurricane underwent <a href="/wiki/Eye_(cyclone)" title="Eye (cyclone)">eyewall replacement cycles</a>, which are internal mechanisms that occur in most intense hurricanes. Daniel later became an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Annular_hurricane" title="Annular hurricane">annular hurricane</a>, which allowed it to maintain Category 4 status for longer than it otherwise would have.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-danialdisc16_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-danialdisc16-29">[28]</a></sup></p>
<p>It crossed over into the Central Pacific early on July 24 and was predicted to affect Hawaii as a tropical storm; however, Daniel encountered weak steering currents in the open ocean, causing it to slow down considerably.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-danieltcr_28-1"><a href="#cite_note-danieltcr-28">[27]</a></sup> It rapidly degenerated to a tropical depression on July 25, and the CPHC issued its last advisory on July 26 while the storm was still well to the east of Hawaii. Its remnants later moved across the Hawaiian islands,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-danieltcr_28-2"><a href="#cite_note-danieltcr-28">[27]</a></sup> dropping heavy rainfall and causing flooding.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cphc_9-1"><a href="#cite_note-cphc-9">[9]</a></sup> West Wailuaiki on Maui recorded 3.87 inches (98 mm) in one day, which was the highest daily rainfall total from the hurricane.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jul06_22-1"><a href="#cite_note-jul06-22">[21]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Storm_Emilia">Tropical Storm Emilia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Tropical Storm Emilia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #00faf4">Tropical storm (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:TS_Emilia_2006.jpg"><img alt="TS Emilia 2006.jpg" data-file-height="4800" data-file-width="4800" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/TS_Emilia_2006.jpg/150px-TS_Emilia_2006.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/TS_Emilia_2006.jpg/225px-TS_Emilia_2006.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/TS_Emilia_2006.jpg/300px-TS_Emilia_2006.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Emilia_2006_track.png"><img alt="Emilia 2006 track.png" data-file-height="633" data-file-width="1024" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Emilia_2006_track.png/150px-Emilia_2006_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Emilia_2006_track.png/225px-Emilia_2006_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Emilia_2006_track.png/300px-Emilia_2006_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>July 21 – July 28</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>65 mph (100 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  990 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Emilia_(2006)" title="Tropical Storm Emilia (2006)">Tropical Storm Emilia (2006)</a></div>
<p>The origins of Emilia were from a <a href="/wiki/Tropical_wave" title="Tropical wave">tropical wave</a> that developed into a tropical depression on July 21, a short distance off the coast of <a href="/wiki/Acapulco" title="Acapulco">Acapulco</a>. It moved generally north-northwestward, reaching tropical storm status on July 22 and passing about 175 mi (280 km) southwest of <a href="/wiki/Manzanillo,_Colima" title="Manzanillo, Colima">Manzanillo, Colima</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-etcr_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-etcr-30">[29]</a></sup> An <a href="/wiki/Eye_(cyclone)" title="Eye (cyclone)">eyewall</a> began to form that day,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[30]</a></sup> and Emilia reached peak winds of 65 mph (105 km/h).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-etcr_30-1"><a href="#cite_note-etcr-30">[29]</a></sup> It briefly weakened due to <a href="/wiki/Wind_shear" title="Wind shear">wind shear</a>, although restrengthening occurred as the storm turned toward the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baja_California_peninsula" title="Baja California peninsula">Baja California peninsula</a>. On July 26, Emilia again reached peak winds of 65 mph (105 km/h), and shortly thereafter it passed about 60 mi (95 km) southwest of the southern tip of Baja California. It weakened as it turned into cooler waters, first to tropical depression status on July 27 and then to a convective-less remnant low on July 28. The remnants dissipated on July 31 about 495 mi (800 km) west-southwest of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/San_Diego,_California" title="San Diego, California">San Diego, California</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-etcr_30-2"><a href="#cite_note-etcr-30">[29]</a></sup></p>
<p>In southwestern Mexico, Emilia produced tropical storm force winds along the coastline. Rainfall in the southern portion of the Baja California peninsula caused minor flooding, and gusty winds caused damage to buildings and power lines.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-etcr_30-3"><a href="#cite_note-etcr-30">[29]</a></sup> Moisture from Emilia reached the southwestern United States. Thunderstorms and rainfall occurred across Arizona, causing flooding.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[31]</a></sup> In southern California, the storm dropped light rainfall, which assisted firefighters in containing a wildfire.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[32]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Storm_Fabio">Tropical Storm Fabio</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Tropical Storm Fabio">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #00faf4">Tropical storm (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tropical_Storm_Fabio_2006.jpg"><img alt="Tropical Storm Fabio 2006.jpg" data-file-height="700" data-file-width="700" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Tropical_Storm_Fabio_2006.jpg/150px-Tropical_Storm_Fabio_2006.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Tropical_Storm_Fabio_2006.jpg/225px-Tropical_Storm_Fabio_2006.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Tropical_Storm_Fabio_2006.jpg/300px-Tropical_Storm_Fabio_2006.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Fabio_2006_track.png"><img alt="Fabio 2006 track.png" data-file-height="633" data-file-width="1024" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Fabio_2006_track.png/150px-Fabio_2006_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Fabio_2006_track.png/225px-Fabio_2006_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Fabio_2006_track.png/300px-Fabio_2006_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>July 31 – August 3</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>50 mph (85 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  1000 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>A tropical wave crossed the west coast of Africa on July 15 and entered the Pacific on July 25. Convection increased on July 28, and at 1800 UTC on July 31 the system became Tropical Depression Seven-E about 980 miles (1,580 km) southwest of the southern tip of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baja_California_peninsula" title="Baja California peninsula">Baja California peninsula</a>. Six hours later, the depression was upgraded to Tropical Storm Fabio. It moved westward due to a ridge to its north, and on August 1 Fabio reached peak winds of 50 mph (85 km/h). Later, the storm began weakening due to increased <a href="/wiki/Wind_shear" title="Wind shear">wind shear</a> and dry air. On August 3, Fabio deteriorated to tropical depression status, and later that day it degenerated into a remnant <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Low_pressure_area" title="Low pressure area">low pressure area</a>. The remnants continued westward, moving across <a href="/wiki/Hawaii" title="Hawaii">Hawaii</a> on August 7.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ftcr_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-ftcr-34">[33]</a></sup></p>
<p>Although Fabio did not impact land, its remnants produced heavy rainfall in Hawaii. In a 24-hour period, 2.89 inches (73 mm) of rainfall was recorded at <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Glenwood,_Hawaii&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Glenwood, Hawaii (page does not exist)">Glenwood</a> on the island of <a href="/wiki/Hawaii_(island)" title="Hawaii (island)">Hawaii</a>; this was the highest daily rainfall total for the month on the island. However, the heaviest precipitation fell on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mount_Wai%CA%BBale%CA%BBale" title="Mount Waiʻaleʻale">Mount Waiʻaleʻale</a> on <a href="/wiki/Kauai" title="Kauai">Kauai</a>, where 15.08 inches (383 mm) fell in 24 hours; this total alone was greater than all other monthly rainfall totals in the state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hawrain_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-hawrain-35">[34]</a></sup> The heavy rainfall flooded the <a href="/wiki/Hanalei_River" title="Hanalei River">Hanalei River</a>, which forced the closure of the Kuhio Highway when a bridge was inundated.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ftcr_34-1"><a href="#cite_note-ftcr-34">[33]</a></sup> On <a href="/wiki/Oahu" title="Oahu">Oahu</a>, the rainfall caused ponding on roadways and flooding along streams. One flooded stream stranded 24 hikers along a trail, all of whom required rescue by helicopter.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[35]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Storm_Gilma">Tropical Storm Gilma</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Tropical Storm Gilma">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #00faf4">Tropical storm (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:TS_Gilma_2006BW.jpg"><img alt="TS Gilma 2006BW.jpg" data-file-height="800" data-file-width="800" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/TS_Gilma_2006BW.jpg/150px-TS_Gilma_2006BW.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/TS_Gilma_2006BW.jpg/225px-TS_Gilma_2006BW.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/TS_Gilma_2006BW.jpg/300px-TS_Gilma_2006BW.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gilma_2006_track.png"><img alt="Gilma 2006 track.png" data-file-height="633" data-file-width="1024" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Gilma_2006_track.png/150px-Gilma_2006_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Gilma_2006_track.png/225px-Gilma_2006_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Gilma_2006_track.png/300px-Gilma_2006_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>August 1 – August 3</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>40 mph (65 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  1004 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>On July 17, a <a href="/wiki/Tropical_wave" title="Tropical wave">tropical wave</a> exited Africa and crossed the Atlantic without developing. On July 25 it entered the Eastern Pacific, gradually developing an area of organized convection. Despite marginally favorable upper-level winds, the system organized enough to be declared a tropical depression on August 1, several hundred miles southwest of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Acapulco,_Mexico" title="Acapulco, Mexico">Acapulco, Mexico</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gTCR_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-gTCR-37">[36]</a></sup> Initially, the depression tracked west-northwestward.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EPAC_HURDAT_8-2"><a href="#cite_note-EPAC_HURDAT-8">[8]</a></sup> Despite wind shear in the area,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[37]</a></sup> the depression was upgraded to Tropical Storm Gilma later on August 1. The wind shear prevented further strengthening or organization, and Gilma weakened to a tropical depression early on August 2.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gTCR_37-1"><a href="#cite_note-gTCR-37">[36]</a></sup> The depression turned westward,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EPAC_HURDAT_8-3"><a href="#cite_note-EPAC_HURDAT-8">[8]</a></sup> and Gilma degenerated into a remnant low by August 4.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gTCR_37-2"><a href="#cite_note-gTCR-37">[36]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hurricane_Hector">Hurricane Hector</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Hurricane Hector">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ffe775">Category 2 hurricane (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_hector_2006.jpg"><img alt="Hurricane hector 2006.jpg" data-file-height="5200" data-file-width="5200" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Hurricane_hector_2006.jpg/150px-Hurricane_hector_2006.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Hurricane_hector_2006.jpg/225px-Hurricane_hector_2006.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Hurricane_hector_2006.jpg/300px-Hurricane_hector_2006.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hector_2006_track.png"><img alt="Hector 2006 track.png" data-file-height="633" data-file-width="1024" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Hector_2006_track.png/150px-Hector_2006_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Hector_2006_track.png/225px-Hector_2006_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Hector_2006_track.png/300px-Hector_2006_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>August 15 – August 23</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>110 mph (175 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  966 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>A tropical wave exited Africa on July 31, and after no development in the Atlantic, it crossed Central America into the northeastern Pacific Ocean on August 10. Convection gradually increased, and a broad <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Low_pressure_area" title="Low pressure area">low pressure area</a> developed about 375 miles (605 km) south of <a href="/wiki/Acapulco" title="Acapulco">Acapulco, Mexico</a> on August 13. The system continued to become organized, and it developed into a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tropical_Cyclone#Tropical_Depression" title="Tropical Cyclone">tropical depression</a> around 1800 <a href="/wiki/Coordinated_Universal_Time" title="Coordinated Universal Time">UTC</a> on August 15 about 650 mi (1,045 km) south-southwest of the southern tip of <a href="/wiki/Baja_California" title="Baja California">Baja California</a>. It moved west-northwestward, located south of a <a href="/wiki/Ridge_(meteorology)" title="Ridge (meteorology)">ridge</a> that extended westward from northern Mexico westward into the Pacific. The depression quickly intensified into Tropical Storm Hector early on August 16.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hectortcr_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hectortcr-39">[38]</a></sup> Hector was able to steadily strengthen, reaching hurricane status at 0600 UTC on August 17. It is estimated that Hector reached its peak intensity of 110 mph (175 km/h) at 0600 UTC on August 18, while centered about 1,035 mi (1,665 km) southwest of the southern tip of Baja California.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EPAC_HURDAT_8-4"><a href="#cite_note-EPAC_HURDAT-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<p>Hector remained a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saffir-Simpson_Hurricane_Scale#Category_2" title="Saffir-Simpson Hurricane Scale">Category 2 hurricane</a> for about 24 hours.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EPAC_HURDAT_8-5"><a href="#cite_note-EPAC_HURDAT-8">[8]</a></sup> Shortly thereafter, it encountered cooler waters and westerly shear,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[39]</a></sup> and Hector steadily weakened until becoming a tropical storm by August 20. Shortly thereafter, the storm reached a weakness in the <a href="/wiki/Subtropical_ridge" title="Subtropical ridge">subtropical ridge</a>, which caused it to move slowly to the northwest. By August 21, deep convection was confined to the northeast portion of the circulation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[40]</a></sup> The shear was not strong enough to completely weaken the tropical cyclone and Hector remained a tropical storm with 50 mph (85 km/h) winds for about 24 hours.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hectortcr_39-1"><a href="#cite_note-Hectortcr-39">[38]</a></sup> After the remaining shower and thunderstorm activity dissipated on August 22, the cyclone turned westward in response to the low-level easterly wind flow.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[41]</a></sup> Hector weakened to a tropical depression at 0000 UTC on August 23, and to a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Low_pressure_area" title="Low pressure area">remnant low</a> six hours later. The remnant circulation of Hector dissipated on August 24 about 750 mi (1,210 km) east of the <a href="/wiki/Hawaiian_Islands" title="Hawaiian Islands">Hawaiian Islands</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[42]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hurricane_Ioke">Hurricane Ioke</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Hurricane Ioke">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ff6060">Category 5 hurricane (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_Ioke,_MODIS_image_on_August_24,_2006,_2155_UTC.jpg"><img alt="Hurricane Ioke, MODIS image on August 24, 2006, 2155 UTC.jpg" data-file-height="4400" data-file-width="4400" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Hurricane_Ioke%2C_MODIS_image_on_August_24%2C_2006%2C_2155_UTC.jpg/150px-Hurricane_Ioke%2C_MODIS_image_on_August_24%2C_2006%2C_2155_UTC.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Hurricane_Ioke%2C_MODIS_image_on_August_24%2C_2006%2C_2155_UTC.jpg/225px-Hurricane_Ioke%2C_MODIS_image_on_August_24%2C_2006%2C_2155_UTC.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Hurricane_Ioke%2C_MODIS_image_on_August_24%2C_2006%2C_2155_UTC.jpg/300px-Hurricane_Ioke%2C_MODIS_image_on_August_24%2C_2006%2C_2155_UTC.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ioke_2006_track.png"><img alt="Ioke 2006 track.png" data-file-height="1476" data-file-width="2000" height="111" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Ioke_2006_track.png/150px-Ioke_2006_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Ioke_2006_track.png/225px-Ioke_2006_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Ioke_2006_track.png/300px-Ioke_2006_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>August 20 – August 27 <small>(<a href="/wiki/2006_Pacific_typhoon_season#Typhoon_Ioke" title="2006 Pacific typhoon season">Exited basin</a>)</small></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>160 mph (260 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  915 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Ioke" title="Hurricane Ioke">Hurricane Ioke</a></div>
<p>The cyclone developed from the <a href="/wiki/Intertropical_Convergence_Zone" title="Intertropical Convergence Zone">Intertropical Convergence Zone</a> on August 20 far to the south of <a href="/wiki/Hawaii" title="Hawaii">Hawaii</a>. Encountering warm waters, little <a href="/wiki/Wind_shear" title="Wind shear">wind shear</a>, and well-defined <a href="/wiki/Outflow_(meteorology)" title="Outflow (meteorology)">outflow</a>, Ioke intensified from a tropical depression to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saffir-Simpson_Hurricane_Scale" title="Saffir-Simpson Hurricane Scale">Category 4</a> status within 48 hours. Late on August 22 it rapidly weakened to Category 2 status before crossing over <a href="/wiki/Johnston_Atoll" title="Johnston Atoll">Johnston Atoll</a>. Two days later favorable conditions again allowed for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rapid_deepening" title="Rapid deepening">rapid strengthening</a>, and Ioke attained Category 5 status on August 25 before crossing the International Date Line. At the time, its <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Barometric_pressure" title="Barometric pressure">barometric pressure</a> was estimated at 915 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>, thus becoming the strongest hurricane on record in the Central Pacific.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cphc_9-2"><a href="#cite_note-cphc-9">[9]</a></sup> As it continued westward its intensity fluctuated, and on August 31 it passed near <a href="/wiki/Wake_Island" title="Wake Island">Wake Island</a> with winds of 155 mph (249 km/h). Ioke gradually weakened as it turned northwestward and northward, and by September 6 it had transitioned into an <a href="/wiki/Extratropical_cyclone" title="Extratropical cyclone">extratropical cyclone</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-iokeatcr_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-iokeatcr-44">[43]</a></sup> By then, the cyclone had lasted 19 days, reaching the equivalent of <a href="/wiki/List_of_Category_5_Pacific_hurricanes" title="List of Category 5 Pacific hurricanes">Category 5</a> status on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saffir-Simpson_Hurricane_Scale" title="Saffir-Simpson Hurricane Scale">Saffir-Simpson Hurricane Scale</a> three times.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cphc_9-3"><a href="#cite_note-cphc-9">[9]</a></sup> The remnants of Ioke accelerated northeastward and ultimately crossed into <a href="/wiki/Alaska" title="Alaska">Alaska</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cattlenet_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-cattlenet-45">[44]</a></sup></p>
<p>Ioke did not affect any permanently populated areas in the Central Pacific or Western Pacific basins as a hurricane or a typhoon. A crew of 12 people stayed in a hurricane-proof bunker on <a href="/wiki/Johnston_Atoll" title="Johnston Atoll">Johnston Atoll</a> during the hurricane's passage; the crew estimated winds reached over 100 mph (160 km/h), which damaged trees on the island but did not impact the island's bird population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cphc_9-4"><a href="#cite_note-cphc-9">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[45]</a></sup> The hurricane left moderate damage on <a href="/wiki/Wake_Island" title="Wake Island">Wake Island</a> totaling $88 million (2006 USD), which resulted from blown off roofs and damaged buildings, although the infrastructure of the island was left intact. All military personnel were evacuated from the island, the first full-scale evacuation of the island since Typhoon Sarah in <a href="/wiki/1967_Pacific_typhoon_season" title="1967 Pacific typhoon season">1967</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-829afpn_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-829afpn-47">[46]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[47]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[48]</a></sup> Later, the extratropical remnants of Ioke produced a severe storm surge along the <a href="/wiki/Alaska" title="Alaska">Alaskan</a> coastline, causing beach erosion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ncdc_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-ncdc-50">[49]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hurricane_Ileana">Hurricane Ileana</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Hurricane Ileana">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ffc140">Category 3 hurricane (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_Ileana_23_aug_2006_1750Z.jpg"><img alt="Hurricane Ileana 23 aug 2006 1750Z.jpg" data-file-height="5000" data-file-width="5000" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Hurricane_Ileana_23_aug_2006_1750Z.jpg/150px-Hurricane_Ileana_23_aug_2006_1750Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Hurricane_Ileana_23_aug_2006_1750Z.jpg/225px-Hurricane_Ileana_23_aug_2006_1750Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Hurricane_Ileana_23_aug_2006_1750Z.jpg/300px-Hurricane_Ileana_23_aug_2006_1750Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ileana_2006_track.png"><img alt="Ileana 2006 track.png" data-file-height="633" data-file-width="1024" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Ileana_2006_track.png/150px-Ileana_2006_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Ileana_2006_track.png/225px-Ileana_2006_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Ileana_2006_track.png/300px-Ileana_2006_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>August 21 – August 27</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>120 mph (195 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  955 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Ileana_(2006)" title="Hurricane Ileana (2006)">Hurricane Ileana (2006)</a></div>
<p>The origins of Hurricane Ileana were from a tropical wave that moved off the coast of Africa on August 8. It entered the Eastern North Pacific on August 16 and developed into a tropical depression on August 21 near <a href="/wiki/Acapulco" title="Acapulco">Acapulco</a>. The depression strengthened into Tropical Storm Ileana six hours after forming. Ileana continued to strengthen, becoming a hurricane in 24 hours and a major hurricane a day after that. Ileana reached its peak intensity of 120 mph (195 km/h) before beginning a slow weakening phase on August 24 when it encountered cooler waters. Ileana weakened a tropical depression on the morning of August 27 and quickly degenerated into a remnant low, dissipating on August 29.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Illeanatcr_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-Illeanatcr-51">[50]</a></sup> As Ileana was heading north along the Mexican coastline, slight rainfall was recorded along the coast.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ileana_Rain_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ileana_Rain-52">[51]</a></sup> There were also reports of hurricane-force winds on <a href="/wiki/Socorro_Island" title="Socorro Island">Socorro Island</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Illeanatcr_51-1"><a href="#cite_note-Illeanatcr-51">[50]</a></sup> One fatality was reported when a man drowned in heavy surf near <a href="/wiki/Cabo_San_Lucas" title="Cabo San Lucas">Cabo San Lucas</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IlleanaDeath_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-IlleanaDeath-53">[52]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hurricane_John">Hurricane John</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Hurricane John">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ff8f20">Category 4 hurricane (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_John_Aug_31_2006.jpg"><img alt="Hurricane John Aug 31 2006.jpg" data-file-height="6000" data-file-width="6000" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Hurricane_John_Aug_31_2006.jpg/150px-Hurricane_John_Aug_31_2006.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Hurricane_John_Aug_31_2006.jpg/225px-Hurricane_John_Aug_31_2006.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Hurricane_John_Aug_31_2006.jpg/300px-Hurricane_John_Aug_31_2006.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:John_2006_track.png"><img alt="John 2006 track.png" data-file-height="633" data-file-width="1024" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/John_2006_track.png/150px-John_2006_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/John_2006_track.png/225px-John_2006_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/John_2006_track.png/300px-John_2006_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>August 28 – September 4</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>130 mph (215 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  948 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_John_(2006)" title="Hurricane John (2006)">Hurricane John (2006)</a></div>
<p>On August 28, a persistent area of low pressure southwest of <a href="/wiki/Acapulco" title="Acapulco">Acapulco</a>, Mexico developed into a tropical depression. Later that day it strengthened into a tropical storm, and it reached hurricane strength 24 hours later on August 29. John underwent rapid intensification and reached Category 3 intensity later that day and Category 4 on August 30.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jtcr_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-jtcr-54">[53]</a></sup> Hours later, the hurricane underwent another eyewall replacement cycle,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-johndisc10_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-johndisc10-55">[54]</a></sup> and subsequently weakened to Category 3 status as it paralleled the Mexican coastline a short distance offshore.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-johndisc11_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-johndisc11-56">[55]</a></sup> Potentially due to its eyewall replacement cycle or its interaction with land, Hurricane John weakened to a 105 mph hurricane by late on August 31,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-john14_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-john14-57">[56]</a></sup> but restrengthened to a major hurricane shortly after. It made landfall near the southern tip of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baja_California_peninsula" title="Baja California peninsula">Baja California peninsula</a> as a Category 2 hurricane on September 1.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-john19_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-john19-58">[57]</a></sup> John continued northwestward along the eastern Baja California peninsula, weakening to tropical depression status by September 3 and dissipating on September 4 in the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_California" title="Gulf of California">Gulf of California</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jtcr_54-1"><a href="#cite_note-jtcr-54">[53]</a></sup></p>
<p>Along the southwestern coast of Mexico, Hurricane John produced heavy surf, strong winds, and heavy rainfall, which flooded roads, caused mudslides, and downed trees.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jtcr_54-2"><a href="#cite_note-jtcr-54">[53]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[58]</a></sup> Along the Baja California Peninsula, the hurricane dropped heavy rainfall, with a 24-hour peak of 10.8 inches (276 mm) in Los Planes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[59]</a></sup> The heavy rainfall caused flooding, closed roads,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lapaz_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-lapaz-61">[60]</a></sup> and caused a dam to overflow.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fourdeaths_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-fourdeaths-62">[61]</a></sup> The winds and rainfall destroyed thousands of flimsy houses across the region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bajadamage_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-bajadamage-63">[62]</a></sup> Across Mexico, five people were killed,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jtcr_54-3"><a href="#cite_note-jtcr-54">[53]</a></sup> and damage amounted to $663 million (2006 <a href="/wiki/Mexican_peso" title="Mexican peso">MXN</a>, $60.8 million 2006 <a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">USD</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mexicodamagetotal_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-mexicodamagetotal-64">[63]</a></sup> Moisture from the remnants of John produced flooding across Texas, which closed a ½ mile (800 m) portion of <a href="/wiki/Interstate_10" title="Interstate 10">Interstate 10</a> in El Paso.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-foxnews_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-foxnews-65">[64]</a></sup> In southern New Mexico, the rainfall caused widespread street flooding and some minor damage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[65]</a></sup> Tropical moisture from the storm also produced rainfall in <a href="/wiki/Arizona" title="Arizona">Arizona</a> and southern <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">California</a>, where eight separate mudslides occurred, trapping 19 vehicles but causing no injuries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-califor_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-califor-67">[66]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hurricane_Kristy">Hurricane Kristy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Hurricane Kristy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Kristy_(2006)" title="Hurricane Kristy (2006)">Hurricane Kristy (2006)</a></div>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ffffcc">Category 1 hurricane (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:12E_Hurricane_Kristy_2006.jpg"><img alt="12E Hurricane Kristy 2006.jpg" data-file-height="4643" data-file-width="4419" height="158" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/12E_Hurricane_Kristy_2006.jpg/150px-12E_Hurricane_Kristy_2006.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/12E_Hurricane_Kristy_2006.jpg/225px-12E_Hurricane_Kristy_2006.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/12E_Hurricane_Kristy_2006.jpg/300px-12E_Hurricane_Kristy_2006.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kristy_2006_track.png"><img alt="Kristy 2006 track.png" data-file-height="633" data-file-width="1024" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Kristy_2006_track.png/150px-Kristy_2006_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Kristy_2006_track.png/225px-Kristy_2006_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Kristy_2006_track.png/300px-Kristy_2006_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>August 30 – September 8</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>80 mph (130 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  985 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>On August 30, a tropical wave located about 525 miles (850 km) south-southwest of <a href="/wiki/Baja_California" title="Baja California">Baja California</a> became more organized and was designated as the twelfth tropical depression of the 2006 season. It strengthened into Tropical Storm Kristy and became Hurricane Kristy the next day. It did not retain this status for long, partly due to its proximity to Hurricane John.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ktcr_68-0"><a href="#cite_note-ktcr-68">[67]</a></sup> There was a possibility of a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fujiwhara_interaction" title="Fujiwhara interaction">Fujiwhara interaction</a> between both systems, causing Kristy to weaken or perhaps be absorbed into the circulation of John.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[68]</a></sup> This did not occur, however. Kristy weakened steadily after its peak intensity and looked to be close to dissipating, but on September 3 and again on September 5, convection flared up and it returned to tropical storm strength.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ktcr_68-1"><a href="#cite_note-ktcr-68">[67]</a></sup> After oscillating between storm and depression strength, the system degenerated into a remnant low on September 7, which dissipated on September 8 without affecting land.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ktcr_68-2"><a href="#cite_note-ktcr-68">[67]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hurricane_Lane">Hurricane Lane</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Hurricane Lane">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ffc140">Category 3 hurricane (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_Lane_16_sept_2006_aqua.jpg"><img alt="Hurricane Lane 16 sept 2006 aqua.jpg" data-file-height="6700" data-file-width="5600" height="179" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Hurricane_Lane_16_sept_2006_aqua.jpg/150px-Hurricane_Lane_16_sept_2006_aqua.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Hurricane_Lane_16_sept_2006_aqua.jpg/225px-Hurricane_Lane_16_sept_2006_aqua.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Hurricane_Lane_16_sept_2006_aqua.jpg/300px-Hurricane_Lane_16_sept_2006_aqua.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lane_2006_track.png"><img alt="Lane 2006 track.png" data-file-height="633" data-file-width="1024" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Lane_2006_track.png/150px-Lane_2006_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Lane_2006_track.png/225px-Lane_2006_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Lane_2006_track.png/300px-Lane_2006_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>September 13 – September 17</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>125 mph (205 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  952 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Lane_(2006)" title="Hurricane Lane (2006)">Hurricane Lane (2006)</a></div>
<p>On September 13, a tropical disturbance located about 125 miles (200 km) west-southwest of <a href="/wiki/Acapulco" title="Acapulco">Acapulco</a>, Mexico, gradually became better organized and was designated the thirteenth tropical depression of the 2006 season. The depression intensified in a favorable environment, and was upgraded to Tropical Storm Lane later that night. As it moved parallel to the Mexican coast it continued to strengthen and became a hurricane on September 15, and a major hurricane early the next day. Hurricane Lane reached peak winds of 125 mph (205 km/h) before it made landfall on the coast of <a href="/wiki/Sinaloa" title="Sinaloa">Sinaloa</a> on September 16. It quickly weakened over land and dissipated on September 17.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ltcr_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-ltcr-70">[69]</a></sup></p>
<p>Tropical Storm Lane produced heavy rainfall and high seas along the west coast of Mexico, including <a href="/wiki/Acapulco" title="Acapulco">Acapulco</a> where flood waters reached 16 inches (40 cm) in depth. The Acapulco airport also experienced flooding, though service was not interrupted.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aplane_71-0"><a href="#cite_note-aplane-71">[70]</a></sup> Throughout Mexico, the hurricane caused four deaths and $2.2 billion (2006 MXN, $203 million 2006 USD) in damage,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sinal_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-sinal-72">[71]</a></sup> half of which in <a href="/wiki/Sinaloa" title="Sinaloa">Sinaloa</a> where heavy crop damage was reported.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sinaloadamagetotal_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-sinaloadamagetotal-73">[72]</a></sup> An estimated 4,320 homes were affected by the hurricane, and 19,200 miles (30,000 km) of roads and highways were damaged to some degree, including some destroyed bridges.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sinal_72-1"><a href="#cite_note-sinal-72">[71]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Storm_Miriam">Tropical Storm Miriam</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2006_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Tropical Storm Miriam">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #00faf4">Tropical storm (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Miriam06.jpg"><img alt="Miriam06.jpg" data-file-height="548" data-file-width="568" height="145" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Miriam06.jpg/150px-Miriam06.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Miriam06.jpg/225px-Miriam06.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Miriam06.jpg/300px-Miriam06.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Miriam_2006_track.png"><img alt="Miriam 2006 track.png" data-file-height="633" data-file-width="1024" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Miriam_2006_track.png/150px-Miriam_2006_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Miriam_2006_track.png/225px-Miriam_2006_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Miriam_2006_track.png/300px-Miriam_2006_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>September 16 – September 18</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>45 mph (75 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  999 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
